<p><b>Donald Ervin Knuth</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="&#39;k&#39; in &#39;kind&#39;">k</span><span title="/ə/ &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;no&#39;">n</span><span title="/uː/ long &#39;oo&#39; in &#39;food&#39;">uː</span><span title="/θ/ &#39;th&#39; in &#39;thigh&#39;">θ</span></span>/</a></span></span><sup id="cite_ref-faq_3-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Knuth#cite_note-faq-3">[3]</a></sup> <span title="English pronunciation respelling"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i>kə-<b><span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">NOOTH</span></span></b></i></a></span>; born January 10, 1938) is an American <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_science" title="Computer science">computer scientist</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematician" title="Mathematician">mathematician</a>, and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Professor_emeritus" class="mw-redirect" title="Professor emeritus">professor emeritus</a> at <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stanford_University" title="Stanford University">Stanford University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-homepage_7-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Knuth#cite_note-homepage-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>He is the author of the multi-volume work <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Art_of_Computer_Programming" title="The Art of Computer Programming">The Art of Computer Programming</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Knuth#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> Knuth has been called the "father of the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Analysis_of_algorithms" title="Analysis of algorithms">analysis of algorithms</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Knuth#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> He contributed to the development of the rigorous analysis of the computational complexity of algorithms and systematized formal mathematical techniques for it. In the process he also popularized the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Big_O_notation" title="Big O notation">asymptotic notation</a>. In addition to fundamental contributions in several branches of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theoretical_computer_science" title="Theoretical computer science">theoretical computer science</a>, Knuth is the creator of the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TeX" title="TeX">TeX</a> computer typesetting system, the related <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/METAFONT" class="mw-redirect" title="METAFONT">METAFONT</a> font definition language and rendering system, and the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_Modern" title="Computer Modern">Computer Modern</a> family of typefaces.</p>
<p>As a writer and scholar,<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Knuth#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> Knuth created the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/WEB" title="WEB">WEB</a> and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CWEB" title="CWEB">CWEB</a> computer programming systems designed to encourage and facilitate <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Literate_programming" title="Literate programming">literate programming</a>, and designed the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MIX" title="MIX">MIX</a>/<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MMIX" title="MMIX">MMIX</a> <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Instruction_set" title="Instruction set">instruction set architectures</a>. As a member of the academic and scientific community, Knuth is strongly opposed to the policy of granting <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Software_patent" title="Software patent">software patents</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Knuth#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> He has expressed his disagreement directly to both the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Patent_and_Trademark_Office" title="United States Patent and Trademark Office">United States Patent and Trademark Office</a> and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Patent_Organization" class="mw-redirect" title="European Patent Organization">European Patent Organization</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Knuth#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Donald_Knuth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1&amp;editintro=Template:BLP_editintro" title="Edit section: Early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Knuth was born in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Milwaukee" title="Milwaukee">Milwaukee</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wisconsin" title="Wisconsin">Wisconsin</a>, to Ervin Henry Knuth and Louise Marie Bohning, of German ancestry.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Knuth#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> His father owned a small printing business and taught bookkeeping at <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Milwaukee_Lutheran_High_School" title="Milwaukee Lutheran High School">Milwaukee Lutheran High School</a>, where Donald enrolled, earning achievement awards. He applied his intelligence in unconventional ways, winning a contest when he was in eighth grade by finding over 4,500 words that could be formed from the letters in "Ziegler's Giant Bar"; the judges had only about 2,500 words on their master list. This won him a television set for his school and enough candy bars for his entire school.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Knuth#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Donald_Knuth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2&amp;editintro=Template:BLP_editintro" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Knuth had a difficult time choosing physics over music as his major at <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Case_Western_Reserve_University" title="Case Western Reserve University">Case Institute of Technology</a> (now part of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Case_Western_Reserve_University" title="Case Western Reserve University">Case Western Reserve University</a>). He also joined Beta Nu Chapter of the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theta_Chi_fraternity" class="mw-redirect" title="Theta Chi fraternity">Theta Chi fraternity</a>. While studying physics at the Case Institute of Technology, Knuth was introduced to the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IBM_650" title="IBM 650">IBM 650</a>, one of the early <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mainframe_computer" title="Mainframe computer">mainframes</a>. After reading the computer's manual, Knuth decided to rewrite the assembly and compiler code for the machine used in his school, because he believed he could do it better.<sup id="cite_ref-Koshy2004_15-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Knuth#cite_note-Koshy2004-15">[15]</a></sup> In 1958, Knuth constructed a program based on the value of each player that could help his school basketball team win the league. This was so novel a proposition at the time that it got picked up and published by <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Newsweek" title="Newsweek">Newsweek</a></i> and also covered by <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Walter_Cronkite" title="Walter Cronkite">Walter Cronkite</a> on the <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CBS_Evening_News" title="CBS Evening News">CBS Evening News</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Koshy2004_15-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Knuth#cite_note-Koshy2004-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>Knuth was one of the founding editors of the <i>Engineering and Science Review</i>, which won a national award as best technical magazine in 1959.<sup id="cite_ref-Beta_Nu_Chapter_16-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Knuth#cite_note-Beta_Nu_Chapter-16">[16]</a></sup> He then switched from physics to mathematics, and in 1960 he received his bachelor of science degree, simultaneously being given a master of science degree by a special award of the faculty who considered his work exceptionally outstanding.<sup id="cite_ref-Koshy2004_15-2" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Knuth#cite_note-Koshy2004-15">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Turing_Award_17-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Knuth#cite_note-Turing_Award-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1963, he earned a PhD in mathematics (his advisor was <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marshall_Hall_(mathematician)" title="Marshall Hall (mathematician)">Marshall Hall</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-mathgene_4-2" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Knuth#cite_note-mathgene-4">[4]</a></sup> from the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California_Institute_of_Technology" title="California Institute of Technology">California Institute of Technology</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Knuth#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_work">Early work</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Donald_Knuth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3&amp;editintro=Template:BLP_editintro" title="Edit section: Early work">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>After receiving his PhD, Knuth joined Caltech's faculty as an associate professor.</p>
<p>He accepted a commission to write a book on computer <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Programming_language" title="Programming language">programming language</a> <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Compiler" title="Compiler">compilers</a>. While working on this project, Knuth decided that he could not adequately treat the topic without first developing a fundamental theory of computer programming, which became <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Art_of_Computer_Programming" title="The Art of Computer Programming">The Art of Computer Programming</a></i>. He originally planned to publish this as a single book. As Knuth developed his outline for the book, he concluded that he required six volumes, and then seven, to thoroughly cover the subject. He published the first volume in 1968.</p>
<p>Just before publishing the first volume of <i>The Art of Computer Programming</i>, Knuth left Caltech to accept employment with the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Institute_for_Defense_Analyses#Center_for_Communications_and_Computing" title="Institute for Defense Analyses">Institute for Defense Analyses' Communications Research Division</a>, then situated on the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Princeton_University" title="Princeton University">Princeton University</a> campus, which was performing mathematical research in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cryptography" title="Cryptography">cryptography</a> to support the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Security_Agency" title="National Security Agency">National Security Agency</a>.</p>
<p>Knuth then left this position to join the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stanford_University" title="Stanford University">Stanford University</a> faculty.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Writings">Writings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Donald_Knuth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4&amp;editintro=Template:BLP_editintro" title="Edit section: Writings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Art_of_Computer_Programming_.28TAOCP.29"><i>The Art of Computer Programming</i> (<i>TAOCP</i>)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Donald_Knuth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5&amp;editintro=Template:BLP_editintro" title="Edit section: The Art of Computer Programming (TAOCP)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Art_of_Computer_Programming" title="The Art of Computer Programming">The Art of Computer Programming</a></div>
<p>Computer science was then taking its first hesitant steps. "It was a totally new field," Knuth recalls, "with no real identity. And the standard of available publications was not that high. A lot of the papers coming out were quite simply wrong. [...] So one of my motivations was to put straight a story that had been very badly told."</p>
<p>After producing the third volume of his series in 1976, he expressed such frustration with the nascent state of the then newly developed electronic publishing tools (especially those that provided input to phototypesetters) that he took time out to work on typesetting and created the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TeX" title="TeX">TeX</a> and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/METAFONT" class="mw-redirect" title="METAFONT">METAFONT</a> tools.</p>
<p>As of 2013<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Donald_Knuth&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the first three volumes and part one of volume four of his series have been published.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Knuth#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Concrete_Mathematics" title="Concrete Mathematics">Concrete Mathematics: A Foundation for Computer Science</a></i> 2nd ed., which originated with an expansion of the mathematical preliminaries section of Volume 1 of <i>TAoCP</i>, has also been published.</p>
<p><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bill_Gates" title="Bill Gates">Bill Gates</a> has praised the difficulty of the subject matter in <i>The Art of Computer Programming</i>, stating that "If you think you're a really good programmer...You should definitely send me a résumé if you can read the whole thing."<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Knuth#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_works">Other works</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Donald_Knuth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6&amp;editintro=Template:BLP_editintro" title="Edit section: Other works">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>He is also the author of <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Surreal_Numbers_(book)" class="mw-redirect" title="Surreal Numbers (book)">Surreal Numbers</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKnuth1974_21-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Knuth#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKnuth1974-21">[21]</a></sup> a mathematical novelette on <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Horton_Conway" title="John Horton Conway">John Conway</a>'s <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Set_theory" title="Set theory">set theory</a> construction of an alternate system of numbers. Instead of simply explaining the subject, the book seeks to show the development of the mathematics. Knuth wanted the book to prepare students for doing original, creative research.</p>
<p>In 1995, Knuth wrote the foreword to the book <i>A=B</i> by <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marko_Petkovsek" class="mw-redirect" title="Marko Petkovsek">Marko Petkovsek</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Herbert_Wilf" title="Herbert Wilf">Herbert Wilf</a> and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Doron_Zeilberger" title="Doron Zeilberger">Doron Zeilberger</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Knuth#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> Knuth is also an occasional contributor of language puzzles to <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Word_Ways:_The_Journal_of_Recreational_Linguistics" class="mw-redirect" title="Word Ways: The Journal of Recreational Linguistics">Word Ways: The Journal of Recreational Linguistics</a></i>.</p>
<p>Knuth has also delved into <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Recreational_mathematics" title="Recreational mathematics">recreational mathematics</a>. He contributed articles to the <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Journal_of_Recreational_Mathematics" title="Journal of Recreational Mathematics">Journal of Recreational Mathematics</a></i> beginning in the 1960s, and was acknowledged as a major contributor in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joseph_Madachy" title="Joseph Madachy">Joseph Madachy</a>'s <i>Mathematics on Vacation</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Knuth#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religious_beliefs_and_work">Religious beliefs and work</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Donald_Knuth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7&amp;editintro=Template:BLP_editintro" title="Edit section: Religious beliefs and work">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In addition to his writings on computer science, Knuth, a <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lutheranism" title="Lutheranism">Lutheran</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPlatoni2006_24-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Knuth#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPlatoni2006-24">[24]</a></sup> is also the author of <i>3:16 Bible Texts Illuminated</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Knuth#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> in which he examines the Bible by a process of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Systematic_sampling" title="Systematic sampling">systematic sampling</a>, namely an analysis of chapter 3, verse 16 of each book. Each verse is accompanied by a rendering in calligraphic art, contributed by a group of calligraphers under the leadership of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hermann_Zapf" title="Hermann Zapf">Hermann Zapf</a>.</p>
<p>Subsequently he was invited to give a set of lectures on his <cite class="citation"><i>3:16</i></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ADonald+Knuth&amp;rft.btitle=3%3A16&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&nbsp;</span></span> project, resulting in another book, <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Things_a_Computer_Scientist_Rarely_Talks_About" title="Things a Computer Scientist Rarely Talks About">Things a Computer Scientist Rarely Talks About</a></i>, where he published the lectures <i>"God and Computer Science"</i>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Health_concerns">Health concerns</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Donald_Knuth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8&amp;editintro=Template:BLP_editintro" title="Edit section: Health concerns">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In 2006, Knuth was diagnosed with <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prostate_cancer" title="Prostate cancer">prostate cancer</a>. He underwent surgery in December that year and started "a little bit of radiation therapy... as a precaution but the prognosis looks pretty good", as he reported in his video autobiography.<sup id="cite_ref-cancer_26-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Knuth#cite_note-cancer-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Computer_musings">Computer musings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Donald_Knuth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9&amp;editintro=Template:BLP_editintro" title="Edit section: Computer musings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Knuth gives informal lectures a few times a year at <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stanford_University" title="Stanford University">Stanford University</a>, which he called Computer Musings. He is a visiting professor at the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oxford_University_Department_of_Computer_Science" class="mw-redirect" title="Oxford University Department of Computer Science">Oxford University Department of Computer Science</a> in the United Kingdom and an Honorary Fellow of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Magdalen_College,_Oxford" title="Magdalen College, Oxford">Magdalen College</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Knuth#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Knuth#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Humor">Humor</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Donald_Knuth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10&amp;editintro=Template:BLP_editintro" title="Edit section: Humor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Knuth-check2.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="./dony_files/220px-Knuth-check2.png" width="220" height="100" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Knuth-check2.png/330px-Knuth-check2.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Knuth-check2.png/440px-Knuth-check2.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="408"></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Knuth-check2.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
One of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Knuth_reward_check" title="Knuth reward check">Knuth's reward checks</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Jacob_Appelbaum_and_Donald_Knuth.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="./dony_files/220px-Jacob_Appelbaum_and_Donald_Knuth.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Jacob_Appelbaum_and_Donald_Knuth.jpg/330px-Jacob_Appelbaum_and_Donald_Knuth.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Jacob_Appelbaum_and_Donald_Knuth.jpg/440px-Jacob_Appelbaum_and_Donald_Knuth.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000"></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Jacob_Appelbaum_and_Donald_Knuth.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
"Nested <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parentheses" class="mw-redirect" title="Parentheses">parens</a>"—<abbr title="The second Donald Knuth is on Jacob Appelbaum&#39;s shirt within the two parentheses">Donald Knuth</abbr> and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jacob_Appelbaum" title="Jacob Appelbaum">Jacob Appelbaum</a> and Donald Knuth</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Knuth used to pay a <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Finder%27s_fee" title="Finder&#39;s fee">finder's fee</a> of $2.56 for any typographical errors or mistakes discovered in his books, because "256 pennies is one <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hexadecimal" title="Hexadecimal">hexadecimal</a> dollar", and $0.32 for "valuable suggestions". According to an article in the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Massachusetts_Institute_of_Technology" title="Massachusetts Institute of Technology">Massachusetts Institute of Technology</a>'s <i>Technology Review</i>, these <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Knuth_reward_check" title="Knuth reward check">Knuth reward checks</a> are "among computerdom's most prized trophies". Knuth had to stop sending real checks in 2008 due to bank fraud, and instead now gives each error finder a "certificate of deposit" from a publicly listed balance in his fictitious "Bank of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/San_Serriffe" title="San Serriffe">San Serriffe</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Knuth#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p>He once warned a correspondent, "Beware of bugs in the above code; I have only proved it correct, not tried it."<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Knuth#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p>Knuth published his first "scientific" article in a school magazine in 1957 under the title "<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Potrzebie" title="Potrzebie">Potrzebie</a> System of Weights and Measures." In it, he defined the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fundamental_unit" class="mw-redirect" title="Fundamental unit">fundamental unit</a> of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Length" title="Length">length</a> as the thickness of <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mad_(magazine)" title="Mad (magazine)">Mad</a></i> No. 26, and named the fundamental unit of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Force" title="Force">force</a> "whatmeworry." <i>Mad</i> published the article in issue No. 33 (June 1957).<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Knuth#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<p>To demonstrate the concept, Knuth intentionally referred "Circular definition" and "Definition, circular" to each other in the index of <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Art_of_Computer_Programming" title="The Art of Computer Programming">The Art of Computer Programming</a>, Volume 1</i>.</p>
<p>At the TUG 2010 Conference, Knuth announced an <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/XML" title="XML">XML</a>-based successor to TeX, titled "iTeX" (<small>pronounced&nbsp;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[iː˨˩˦tɛks˧˥]</a></span>, with a bell ringing), which would support features such as arbitrarily scaled irrational units, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/3D_printing" title="3D printing">3D printing</a>, animation, and stereophonic sound.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Knuth#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Knuth#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Knuth#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_and_honors">Awards and honors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Donald_Knuth&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11&amp;editintro=Template:BLP_editintro" title="Edit section: Awards and honors">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In 1971, Knuth was the recipient of the first <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Association_for_Computing_Machinery" title="Association for Computing Machinery">ACM</a> <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grace_Murray_Hopper_Award" title="Grace Murray Hopper Award">Grace Murray Hopper Award</a>. He has received various other awards including the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turing_Award" title="Turing Award">Turing Award</a>, the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Medal_of_Science" title="National Medal of Science">National Medal of Science</a>, the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann_Medal" class="mw-redirect" title="John von Neumann Medal">John von Neumann Medal</a>, and the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kyoto_Prize" title="Kyoto Prize">Kyoto Prize</a>.</p>
<p>In recognition of Knuth's contributions to the field of computer science, in 1990 he was awarded the one-of-a-kind academic title of <i>Professor of The Art of Computer Programming</i>, which has since been revised to <i>Professor <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emeritus" title="Emeritus">Emeritus</a> of The Art of Computer Programming</i>.</p>
<p>Knuth was elected to the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Academy_of_Sciences" title="National Academy of Sciences">National Academy of Sciences</a> in 1975. In 1992, he became an associate of the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_Academy_of_Sciences" title="French Academy of Sciences">French Academy of Sciences</a>. Also that year, he retired from regular research and teaching at <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stanford_University" title="Stanford University">Stanford University</a> in order to finish <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Art_of_Computer_Programming" title="The Art of Computer Programming">The Art of Computer Programming</a></i>. He was elected a <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Fellows_of_the_Royal_Society_elected_in_2003" title="List of Fellows of the Royal Society elected in 2003">Foreign Member of the Royal Society (ForMemRS) in 2003</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-formemrs_6-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Knuth#cite_note-formemrs-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>Knuth was elected as a Fellow (first class of Fellows) of the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Society_for_Industrial_and_Applied_Mathematics" title="Society for Industrial and Applied Mathematics">Society for Industrial and Applied Mathematics</a> in 2009 for his outstanding contributions to mathematics.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Knuth#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> He is a member of the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Norwegian_Academy_of_Science_and_Letters" title="Norwegian Academy of Science and Letters">Norwegian Academy of Science and Letters</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Knuth#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> In 2012, he became a fellow of the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Mathematical_Society" title="American Mathematical Society">American Mathematical Society</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Knuth#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> Other awards and honors include:</p>
<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 35em; -webkit-column-width: 35em; column-width: 35em;">
<ul>
<li>First <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Association_for_Computing_Machinery" title="Association for Computing Machinery">ACM</a> <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grace_Murray_Hopper_Award" title="Grace Murray Hopper Award">Grace Murray Hopper Award</a>, 1971</li>
<li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turing_Award" title="Turing Award">Turing Award</a>, 1974</li>
<li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lester_R._Ford_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Lester R. Ford Award">Lester R. Ford Award</a>, 1975<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Knuth#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> and 1993<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Knuth#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></li>
<li>Josiah Willard Gibbs Lecturer, 1978<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Knuth#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Knuth#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Medal_of_Science" title="National Medal of Science">National Medal of Science</a>, 1979</li>
<li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_Medal" title="Franklin Medal">Franklin Medal</a>, 1988</li>
<li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_von_Neumann_Medal" class="mw-redirect" title="John von Neumann Medal">John von Neumann Medal</a>, 1995</li>
<li>Harvey Prize from the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Technion_%E2%80%93_Israel_Institute_of_Technology" title="Technion – Israel Institute of Technology">Technion</a>, 1995<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Knuth#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kyoto_Prize" title="Kyoto Prize">Kyoto Prize</a>, 1996</li>
<li>Fellow of the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_History_Museum" title="Computer History Museum">Computer History Museum</a> "for his fundamental early work in the history of computing algorithms, development of the TeX typesetting language, and for major contributions to mathematics and computer science." 1998<sup id="cite_ref-ComputerHistory_5-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Knuth#cite_note-ComputerHistory-5">[5]</a></sup></li>
<li>Katayanagi Prize, 2010<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Knuth#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BBVA_Foundation_Frontiers_of_Knowledge_Award" title="BBVA Foundation Frontiers of Knowledge Award">BBVA Foundation Frontiers of Knowledge Award</a> in the category of Information and Communication Technologies, 2010<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Knuth#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turing_Lecture" title="Turing Lecture">Turing Lecture</a>, 2011</li>
<li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stanford_University_School_of_Engineering" title="Stanford University School of Engineering">Stanford University School of Engineering</a> Hero Award, 2011<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Knuth#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
</div>

<li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robinson%E2%80%93Schensted%E2%80%93Knuth_correspondence" title="Robinson–Schensted–Knuth correspondence">Robinson–Schensted–Knuth correspondence</a></li>
<li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trabb_Pardo%E2%80%93Knuth_algorithm" title="Trabb Pardo–Knuth algorithm">Trabb Pardo–Knuth algorithm</a></li>
